[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The statement `w.length = 0 ↔ w = []` is essentially the well-known list property that a list has length zero if and only if it is empty. Since `Word α` is defined as `List α` and `Word.length` is defined as `List.length`, the theorem is exactly `List.length_eq_zero` from `Mathlib.Data.List.Basic`, which is already imported via `CoW.Word`. No further reasoning or additional lemmas are required; the proof is a direct application of this existing lemma.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Directly prove the theorem by applying the existing lemma `List.length_eq_zero` to `w`. 

   Since `Word.length` is an abbreviation for `List.length`, the goal `w.length = 0 ↔ w = []` is definitionally equivalent to `List.length w = 0 ↔ w = []`. The lemma `List.length_eq_zero` (from `Mathlib.Data.List.Basic`) already provides exactly this equivalence.

The theorem `word_concat_right_cancel` states that concatenation on the right is cancellative: if `u ++ w = v ++ w`, then `u = v`. Since `Word α` is `List α` and `⬝` is `List.append`, this is exactly the list property `List.append_right_cancel`. The standard Mathlib lemma `List.append_right_cancel` (from `Mathlib.Data.List.Basic`) provides this directly for any `List α`, including our `Word α`.

   Because `⬝` is definitionally `List.append`, the hypothesis is exactly `u ++ w = v ++ w`.  
   The lemma `List.append_right_cancel` yields `u = v`, which completes the proof.

[ 4/45]           Word | MEDIUM | word_concat_left_cancel

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for word_concat_left_cancel
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem is about left cancellation of word concatenation: if `w ⬝ u = w ⬝ v` then `u = v`. Since `Word α` is `List α` and `⬝` is `List.append`, this is a standard list property. It can be proved directly by induction on `w` without needing an external lemma. The base case uses the existing `simp` lemma `Word.concat_empty_left`, and the inductive step uses `injection` (or `List.cons_inj`) to strip the common prefix.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Prove the statement by induction on `w : Word α`.  
   - Base case `w = []`:  
     The hypothesis `h : [] ⬝ u = [] ⬝ v` simplifies to `u = v` by `Word.concat_empty_left` (or directly via `simp`).  
   - Inductive case `w = a :: w'`:  
     The hypothesis becomes `(a :: w') ⬝ u = (a :: w') ⬝ v`.  
     Unfold `⬝` (which is `List.append`), reducing to  
     `a :: (w' ++ u) = a :: (w' ++ v)`.  
     Using `injection` (or `List.cons_inj`) we obtain `w' ++ u = w' ++ v`.  
     Then apply the induction hypothesis for `w'` to conclude `u = v`.

[ 6/45]           Word | MEDIUM | word_pow_succ_left

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for word_pow_succ_left
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem asserts that `w ^ (n+1) = w ⬝ w ^ n`. The library already provides the lemma `Word.pow_succ : w ^ (n+1) = w ^ n ⬝ w`, which is a right-concatenation form. We need to show the left-concatenation form. This follows from the fact that powers of the same word commute: `w ^ m ⬝ w ^ n = w ^ n ⬝ w ^ m`. The library provides `Word.pow_add w m n : w ^ (m+n) = w ^ m ⬝ w ^ n`. Taking `m=1` gives `w ^ (1+n) = w ^ 1 ⬝ w ^ n = w ⬝ w ^ n`. By commutativity of addition `n+1 = 1+n`, we obtain `w ^ (n+1) = w ^ (1+n) = w ⬝ w ^ n`. So the proof can be done using `Nat.add_comm`, `Word.pow_add`, and `Word.pow_one`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Rewrite `w ^ (n+1)` as `w ^ (1+n)` using `Nat.add_comm n 1` (or `Nat.add_comm 1 n`).  
2. Apply `Word.pow_add w 1 n` to rewrite `w ^ (1+n)` as `w ^ 1 ⬝ w ^ n`.  
3. Simplify `w ^ 1` to `w` using `Word.pow_one w`.  
4. This yields exactly the goal `w ⬝ w ^ n`.


--- Builder Execution (Attempt 1/3) ---
[Orchestrator] ⚠️  Proof contains 'sorry' — treating as incomplete.
[Orchestrator] Applying Patch...
```lean4
calc
    w ^ (n + 1) = w ^ (1 + n) := by rw [Nat.add_comm n 1]
    _ = w ^ 1 ⬝ w ^ n := by rw [Word.pow_add]
    _ = w ⬝ w ^ n := by rw [Word.pow_one]
```

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for prefix_of_concat
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is `u ≤ₚ (u ⬝ v)`, where `≤ₚ` is the `IsPrefix` relation. The library provides `IsPrefix.def u (u ⬝ v)` which states the equivalence `(u ≤ₚ u ⬝ v) ↔ ∃ w, u ⬝ v = u ++ w`. Taking `w := v` yields a direct proof because `u ++ v` is exactly `u ⬝ v`. So we can close the goal with `(IsPrefix.def u (u ⬝ v)).mpr ⟨v, rfl⟩`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Apply the lemma `IsPrefix.def` to `u` and `u ⬝ v`. This lemma gives an equivalence: `u ≤ₚ (u ⬝ v) ↔ ∃ w, (u ⬝ v) = u ++ w`.
2. Use the `.mpr` direction of the equivalence with the witness `w := v`.
3. The equality `(u ⬝ v) = u ++ v` holds definitionally because `⬝` is `List.append`. So `rfl` suffices.
4. This directly yields the goal.

obtain ⟨v, hw⟩ := (IsPrefix.def u w).mp h1
  obtain ⟨v', hu⟩ := (IsPrefix.def w u).mp h2
  have h_comb : u = u ++ (v ++ v') := by

      u = w ++ v' := hu
      _ = (u ++ v) ++ v' := by rw [hw]
      _ = u ++ (v ++ v') := by rw [List.append_assoc]
  have hlen_comb := congrArg Word.length h_comb
  simp [Word.length_concat] at hlen_comb
  have hsum : v.length + v'.length = 0 := by
    have htemp : u.length + 0 = u.length + (v.length + v'.length) := by
      simpa [Nat.add_zero] using hlen_comb

  have hv : v = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp hvlen
  have hv' : v' = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp hv'len

  exact hu.symm

      _ = (u ++ v) ++ v' := by rw [← hw]
      _ = u ++ (v ++ v') := by rw [List.append_assoc]
  have hlen_comb := congrArg List.length h_comb
  simp [List.length_append] at hlen_comb
  have hsum : v.length + v'.length = 0 := by omega
  rcases Nat.add_eq_zero_iff.mp hsum with ⟨hvlen, hv'len⟩
  have hv : v = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp hvlen
  have hv' : v' = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp hv'len
  rw [hv, hv'] at hw hu
  simp at hw hu
  exact hu.symm

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 3/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The suffix relation `≤ₛ` is defined as `List.IsSuffix`. The hypotheses `h1 : u ≤ₛ w` and `h2 : w ≤ₛ u` give `w = v ++ u` and `u = v' ++ w` for some `v`, `v'`. Combining these yields `u = (v' ++ v) ++ u`. Taking lengths we deduce `v' ++ v = []`, hence `v = []` and `v' = []`, and finally `u = w`. This proof uses only basic list lemmas that are all available in `Mathlib.Data.List.Basic`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Apply `IsSuffix.def u w` to `h1` to obtain `⟨v, hv⟩` such that `hv : w = v ++ u`.
2. Apply `IsSuffix.def w u` to `h2` to obtain `⟨v', hv'⟩` such that `hv' : u = v' ++ w`.
3. Substitute `hv` into `hv'` to get `u = v' ++ (v ++ u)`. Rewrite with `List.append_assoc` to obtain `u = (v' ++ v) ++ u`.
4. Compute lengths using `List.length_append`:
   - From `u = (v' ++ v) ++ u` we have `u.length = (v' ++ v).length + u.length`.
   - Subtract `u.length` from both sides (using `omega` or `Nat.add_left_cancel` after rewriting) to get `(v' ++ v).length = 0`.
5. Apply `List.length_eq_zero` to get `v' ++ v = []`.
6. Use `List.append_eq_nil` on this to obtain `h_v' : v' = []` and `h_v : v = []`.
7. Substitute `h_v` into `hv` to get `w = [] ++ u` and simplify (by `simp`) to `w = u`.
8. `rw` or `symm` to conclude `u = w`.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal `proper_prefix_irrefl w` states that a word cannot be a proper prefix of itself. By definition `IsProperPrefix u w` is `u ≤ₚ w ∧ u ≠ w`. Hence assuming `w <ₚ w` would give `w ≠ w`, a contradiction. However, the previous attempt using `h.2 rfl` may have failed for some reason. A more explicit proof can be given by unfolding `IsProperPrefix.def` which gives a witness that `w = w ++ v` with `v ≠ []`. Then we can derive `v = []` via `List.append_left_cancel`, contradicting `v ≠ []`. This uses well-known Mathlib lemmas and avoids a direct pair projection.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Assume `h : w <ₚ w`.
2. Apply `(IsProperPrefix.def w w).mp h` to obtain `⟨v, hw, hv⟩` where `hw : w = w ++ v` and `hv : v ≠ []`.
3. From `hw`, derive `w ++ v = w ++ []`:
   - `calc
        w ++ v = w := by rw [hw]
        _ = w ++ [] := by simp
     `
   This gives an equality `w ++ v = w ++ []`.
4. Apply `List.append_left_cancel` to this equality to obtain `v = []`.
5. `hv` contradicts `v = []`. Therefore `¬ (w <ₚ w)`.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is to prove transitivity of `IsProperPrefix`. By definition, `u <ₚ v` is `u ≤ₚ v ∧ u ≠ v`. The prefix parts can be combined using `IsPrefix.trans`. For the inequality `u ≠ w`, we use the antisymmetry of `≤ₚ`: if `u = w`, then from `v ≤ₚ w` we get `v ≤ₚ u`, and together with `u ≤ₚ v` we obtain `u = v` by `List.IsPrefix.antisymm`, contradicting `u ≠ v`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Destructure `huv` into `hpre_uv : u ≤ₚ v` and `hne_uv : u ≠ v`.
   Destructure `hvw` into `hpre_vw : v ≤ₚ w` and `hne_vw : v ≠ w`.
2. Obtain `hpre_uw : u ≤ₚ w` using `IsPrefix.trans hpre_uv hpre_vw`.
3. Show `u ≠ w` by contradiction: assume `h_eq : u = w`. Then rewrite `hpre_vw` to get `v ≤ₚ u`.
   Apply `List.IsPrefix.antisymm hpre_uv` to this, obtaining `u = v`.
   This contradicts `hne_uv`.
4. Combine `hpre_uw` and the inequality proof as `⟨hpre_uw, λ h_eq => hne_uv (List.IsPrefix.antisymm hpre_uv (by rwa [h_eq] at hpre_vw))⟩`.

Substituting gives `w = u ++ (x ++ y)`. The concatenation `x ++ y` is non‑empty because `x ≠ []`. Hence `u` is a proper prefix of `w` by `IsProperPrefix.def`. The needed lemmas are `IsProperPrefix.def`, `List.append_assoc`, and `List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil` (or a direct argument that `x ++ y = []` would force `x = []`).

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

2. Obtain the decomposition of `hvw` using `(IsProperPrefix.def v w).mp hvw`:
   `⟨y, hw_eq, hy_ne⟩` where `hw_eq : w = v ++ y` and `hy_ne : y ≠ []`.
3. Substitute `hv_eq` into `hw_eq`:
   `w = (u ++ x) ++ y = u ++ (x ++ y)` by `List.append_assoc`.
4. Show that `x ++ y ≠ []`:
   - If `x ++ y = []`, then `x = []` by `List.append_eq_nil.mp` (or its left component). This contradicts `hx_ne`.
   So `hxy_ne : x ++ y ≠ []`.
5. Apply `(IsProperPrefix.def u w).mpr` with witness `x ++ y`:
   - The first condition `w = u ++ (x ++ y)` is exactly `calc` from step 3.
   - The second condition `x ++ y ≠ []` is `hxy_ne`.
   This yields `u <ₚ w`.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We need to prove `u <ₚ (u ⬝ v)` assuming `v ≠ []`. The relation `u <ₚ (u ⬝ v)` is defined as `u ≤ₚ (u ⬝ v) ∧ u ≠ u ⬝ v`. The prefix part is exactly the existing lemma `prefix_of_concat u v`. The inequality `u ≠ u ⬝ v` follows by a length argument: if `u = u ⬝ v`, then by `Word.length_concat` we have `u.length = u.length + v.length`. The equation `u.length + v.length = u.length` forces `v.length = 0` by `Nat.eq_zero_of_add_eq_self_left`, and then `List.length_eq_zero` gives `v = []`, contradicting `hv`. Thus we combine the two parts.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

2. Prove `hne : u ≠ u ⬝ v`. Assume `h_eq : u = u ⬝ v`. Compute lengths:
   - `have h_len : u.length = (u ⬝ v).length := congr_arg Word.length h_eq`
   - `rw [Word.length_concat] at h_len` to get `u.length = u.length + v.length`
   - Apply `Nat.eq_zero_of_add_eq_self_left` to `h_len.symm` to obtain `v.length = 0`.
   - Apply `List.length_eq_zero.mp` to this to get `v = []`, which contradicts `hv`.
3. Assemble the result: `exact ⟨hpre, hne⟩`.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem asserts transitivity of proper suffix. From `huv : u <ₛ v` we have `u ≤ₛ v` and `u ≠ v`; from `hvw : v <ₛ w` we have `v ≤ₛ w` and `v ≠ w`. The suffix part `u ≤ₛ w` follows from `IsSuffix.trans`. For the inequality `u ≠ w`, assume `u = w`. Then `hvw` becomes `v <ₛ u`. Using `IsProperSuffix.length_lt` from the lemma in `ProperSuffix.lean` we get `u.length < v.length` from `huv` and `v.length < u.length` from `hvu`. These contradict each other via `Nat.lt_asymm`. Thus `u ≠ w`. This yields `u <ₛ w`.

   - Apply `IsProperSuffix.length_lt` to `hvu` to get `h_len_vu : v.length < u.length`.
   - Use `Nat.lt_asymm h_len_uv h_len_vu` to obtain a contradiction.
4. Return `⟨h_suf_uw, hne_uw⟩`, which is `u <ₛ w`.

   - Compute `h_len := congr_arg Word.length heq`, giving `u.length = (v ⬝ u).length`.
   - Rewrite with `Word.length_concat` at `h_len` to get `u.length = v.length + u.length`.
   - Add `u.length` to both sides suitably: `calc
        u.length + 0 = u.length := by simp
        _ = v.length + u.length := by rw [← h_len]
     `, obtaining `h_sum : u.length + 0 = v.length + u.length`.
   - Apply `Nat.add_left_cancel` to `h_sum` (since both sides have `+ u.length`, we can cancel? Actually `Nat.add_left_cancel` works on the left-hand summand: `a + b = a + c → b = c`. Here we have `u.length + 0 = v.length + u.length`. But the summands on the right are `v.length` and `u.length`. To cancel `u.length`, we need to rearrange: `u.length + 0 = u.length + v.length`. From `h_len` we have `u.length = v.length + u.length`, which by commutativity is `u.length = u.length + v.length`. Then `u.length + 0 = u.length + v.length`. Then `Nat.add_left_cancel` gives `0 = v.length`. So `hv_len0 : v.length = 0`.)  
   Actually simpler: from `h_len` we have `v.length + u.length = u.length`. Rewrite as `u.length + v.length = u.length + 0` (by `simp` on RHS). Then `Nat.add_left_cancel` yields `v.length = 0`. Call this `hv_len0`.
   - Apply `List.length_eq_zero.mp` to `hv_len0` to get `v = []`.
   - This contradicts `hv`. Therefore `hne`.
3. Return `⟨hsuf, hne⟩`, which is `u <ₛ (v ⬝ u)`.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
<plan>
Goal: Prove `IsBorder b₁ w` given `h1 : IsBorder b₁ b₂` and `h2 : IsBorder b₂ w`.

Recall `IsBorder b w` is defined as `b <ₚ w ∧ b <ₛ w`. We need to show both proper prefix and proper suffix transitivity.

**Proper prefix part (`b₁ <ₚ w`):**
1. Extract `h1_pre : b₁ <ₚ b₂` from `h1.1` and `h2_pre : b₂ <ₚ w` from `h2.1`.
2. Apply `(IsProperPrefix.def b₁ b₂).mp h1_pre` to obtain `⟨x, hx_eq, hx_ne⟩` where `hx_eq : b₂ = b₁ ++ x` and `hx_ne : x ≠ []`.
3. Apply `(IsProperPrefix.def b₂ w).mp h2_pre` to obtain `⟨y, hy_eq, hy_ne⟩` where `hy_eq : w = b₂ ++ y` and `hy_ne : y ≠ []`.
4. Show `b₁ <ₚ w` using `(IsProperPrefix.def b₁ w).mpr`:
   - Witness `x ++ y`.
   - Equality: `w = b₁ ++ (x ++ y)`:
     ```
     w = b₂ ++ y        := hy_eq
     _ = (b₁ ++ x) ++ y := by rw [hx_eq]
     _ = b₁ ++ (x ++ y) := by rw [List.append_assoc]
     ```
   - Show `x ++ y ≠ []`.  Assume `h : x ++ y = []`. Then `List.append_eq_nil.mp h` gives `x = []` and `y = []`. The first contradicts `hx_ne`.  Hence `x ++ y ≠ []`.
5. This yields `h_pre_w : b₁ <ₚ w`.

**Proper suffix part (`b₁ <ₛ w`):**
1. Extract `h1_suf : b₁ <ₛ b₂` from `h1.2` and `h2_suf : b₂ <ₛ w` from `h2.2`.
2. Apply `(IsProperSuffix.iff b₁ b₂).mp h1_suf` to obtain `⟨u, hu_eq, hu_ne⟩` where `hu_eq : b₂ = u ++ b₁` and `hu_ne : u ≠ []`.
3. Apply `(IsProperSuffix.iff b₂ w).mp h2_suf` to obtain `⟨v, hv_eq, hv_ne⟩` where `hv_eq : w = v ++ b₂` and `hv_ne : v ≠ []`.
4. Show `b₁ <ₛ w` using `(IsProperSuffix.iff b₁ w).mpr`:
   - Witness `v ++ u`.
   - Equality: 
     ```
     w = v ++ b₂        := hv_eq
     _ = v ++ (u ++ b₁) := by rw [hu_eq]
     _ = (v ++ u) ++ b₁ := by rw [List.append_assoc]
     ```
   - Show `v ++ u ≠ []`.  Assume `h : v ++ u = []`. Then `v = []` and `u = []` by `List.append_eq_nil.mp h`. The first contradicts `hv_ne`. Hence `v ++ u ≠ []`.
5. This yields `h_suf_w : b₁ <ₛ w`.

Combine `h_pre_w` and `h_suf_w` into `⟨h_pre_w, h_suf_w⟩` to prove `IsBorder b₁ w`.<plan>
1. Destructure `h1 : IsBorder b₁ b₂` into `h1_pre : b₁ <ₚ b₂` and `h1_suf : b₁ <ₛ b₂`.
2. Destructure `h2 : IsBorder b₂ w` into `h2_pre : b₂ <ₚ w` and `h2_suf : b₂ <ₛ w`.
3. Prove `h_pre_w : b₁ <ₚ w`:

   - Obtain `⟨y, hy_eq, hy_ne⟩` from `(IsProperPrefix.def b₂ w).mp h2_pre`.
   - Show `w = b₁ ++ (x ++ y)`:
     ```

     _ = (b₁ ++ x) ++ y := by rw [hx_eq]
     _ = b₁ ++ (x ++ y) := by rw [List.append_assoc]
     ```
   - Show `x ++ y ≠ []`. Assume `h : x ++ y = []`. Using `List.append_eq_nil.mp h`, get `x = []`. This contradicts `hx_ne`.
   - Apply `(IsProperPrefix.def b₁ w).mpr ⟨x ++ y, the equality, the non-nil⟩` to obtain `h_pre_w`.
4. Prove `h_suf_w : b₁ <ₛ w`:
   - Obtain `⟨u, hu_eq, hu_ne⟩` from `(IsProperSuffix.iff b₁ b₂).mp h1_suf`.
   - Obtain `⟨v, hv_eq, hv_ne⟩` from `(IsProperSuffix.iff b₂ w).mp h2_suf`.
   - Show `w = (v ++ u) ++ b₁`:
     ```
     w = v ++ b₂       := hv_eq
     _ = v ++ (u ++ b₁) := by rw [hu_eq]
     _ = (v ++ u) ++ b₁ := by rw [List.append_assoc]
     ```
   - Show `v ++ u ≠ []`. Similar argument using `hv_ne` and `List.append_eq_nil.mp`.
   - Apply `(IsProperSuffix.iff b₁ w).mpr ⟨v ++ u, the equality, the non-nil⟩` to obtain `h_suf_w`.
5. Return `⟨h_pre_w, h_suf_w⟩`.
</plan>

   - Show `x ++ y ≠ []` using `List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil hx_ne`.

rcases h2 with ⟨h2pre, h2suf⟩
have hpre_w : b₁ <ₚ w := by

    rw [hy_eq, hx_eq, List.append_assoc]

    intro h
    apply hx_ne
    exact (List.append_eq_nil.1 h).1
  exact (IsProperPrefix.def b₁ w).mpr ⟨x ++ y, h_eq, h_ne⟩

  rcases (IsProperSuffix.iff b₂ w).mp h2suf with ⟨v, hv_eq, hv_ne⟩

    rw [hv_eq, hu_eq, List.append_assoc]
  have h_ne : v ++ u ≠ [] := by
    intro h
    apply hv_ne
    exact (List.append_eq_nil.1 h).1
  exact (IsProperSuffix.iff b₁ w).mpr ⟨v ++ u, h_eq, h_ne⟩
exact ⟨hpre_w, hsuf_w⟩

[34/45]      Conjugacy |   HARD | conjugate_trans

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for conjugate_trans
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
To prove transitivity of word conjugacy `u ~ v` and `v ~ w` implies `u ~ w`, we rely on the classic combinatorial characterization of conjugacy: there exist `x, y` such that `u = x ⬝ y` and `v = y ⬝ x`, and similarly for `v` and `w`. Expanding these definitions gives two equations for `v`:
- `v = y1 ⬝ x1` from `h1`
- `v = x2 ⬝ y2` from `h2`
Thus `y1 ⬝ x1 = x2 ⬝ y2`. Since `⬝` is defined as `List.append`, this is an equality of lists, and we can apply `List.append_eq_append_iff` (Levi's lemma) to obtain two possible cases. In each case we construct a new decomposition of `u` and `w` that demonstrates conjugacy. No additional induction or heavy theory is required because the characterisation of factor overlaps is directly handled by the existing Mathlib lemma.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1.  **Unpack the hypotheses:**
    - `rcases h1 with ⟨x1, y1, hu, hv⟩` where `hu : u = x1 ⬝ y1`, `hv : v = y1 ⬝ x1`.
    - `rcases h2 with ⟨x2, y2, hv', hw⟩` where `hv' : v = x2 ⬝ y2`, `hw : w = y2 ⬝ x2`.

2.  **Extract the common equality:**
    - From `hv` and `hv'` we have `y1 ⬝ x1 = x2 ⬝ y2`.
    - Unfold `Word.concat` (which is `List.append`) to expose the list structure, e.g. `simpa [Word.concat]` or `change y1 ++ x1 = x2 ++ y2 at ...`.

3.  **Apply Levi's lemma:**
    - Use `List.append_eq_append_iff.mp` on the equality `y1 ++ x1 = x2 ++ y2`.
    - This yields a disjunction of two cases.

4.  **Case analysis:**

    **Case 1:** `∃ t, y1 ++ t = x2 ∧ x1 = t ++ y2`.
    - `rcases` to obtain `t` and the two equations.
    - Construct witnesses for `u ~ w`:
        - Let `X := t`, `Y := y2 ++ y1`.
    - Verify `u = X ++ Y`:
        - `u = x1 ++ y1` (by `hu`).
        - Replace `x1` with `t ++ y2`: `(t ++ y2) ++ y1`.
        - Reassociate using `List.append_assoc` to `t ++ (y2 ++ y1)`.
    - Verify `w = Y ++ X`:
        - `w = y2 ++ x2` (by `hw`).
        - Replace `x2` with `y1 ++ t`: `y2 ++ (y1 ++ t)`.
        - Reassociate to `(y2 ++ y1) ++ t`.
    - Conclude `u ~ w` with `⟨X, Y, ...⟩`.

    **Case 2:** `∃ t, y1 = x2 ++ t ∧ t ++ x1 = y2`.
    - `rcases` to obtain `t` and the two equations.
    - Construct witnesses for `u ~ w`:
        - Let `X := x1 ++ x2`, `Y := t`.
    - Verify `u = X ++ Y`:
        - `u = x1 ++ y1`.
        - Replace `y1` with `x2 ++ t`: `x1 ++ (x2 ++ t)`.
        - Reassociate to `(x1 ++ x2) ++ t`.
    - Verify `w = Y ++ X`:
        - `w = y2 ++ x2`.
        - Replace `y2` with `t ++ x1`: `(t ++ x1) ++ x2`.
        - Reassociate to `t ++ (x1 ++ x2)`.
    - Conclude `u ~ w` with `⟨X, Y, ...⟩`.

5.  **Synthesize the goal:**
    - In both cases provide `∃ (x y : Word α), u = x ⬝ y ∧ w = y ⬝ x` using the constructed `X` and `Y`.
    - Rewrite back to `⬝` notation (if needed) using `Word.concat` again, or directly state the equalities over `List.append` and then `simpa [Word.concat]` to obtain the final form.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The previous implementation attempt may have failed due to subtle issues with the translation between `Word.concat` (notation `⬝`) and `List.append` (notation `++`), or with the use of `calc` blocks inside an existential constructor. To make the proof more robust, I will restructure it with explicit `simpa [Word.concat]` steps and isolated `rw`/`simp` reasoning. I'll also double-check the pattern of `List.append_eq_append_iff` to ensure the case splitting is correctly handled. The core mathematical idea remains unchanged: apply Levi's lemma to the equation `y1 ⬝ x1 = x2 ⬝ y2` obtained from the two conjugacy decompositions, then construct the new witnesses for `u ~ w` in each of the two resulting cases.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1.  **Unpack the hypotheses** (same as before):
    ```lean4
    rcases h1 with ⟨x1, y1, hu, hv⟩
    rcases h2 with ⟨x2, y2, hv', hw⟩
    ```

2.  **Create the common equation in `List` form:**
    ```lean4
    have h_eq : y1 ++ x1 = x2 ++ y2 := by
      simpa [Word.concat] using congrArg (fun t => t) (by rw [hv, hv'])
    ```
    A safer alternative is:
    ```lean4
    have h_eq : y1 ++ x1 = x2 ++ y2 := by
      -- from hv: v = y1 ⬝ x1, hv': v = x2 ⬝ y2
      calc
        y1 ++ x1 = y1 ⬝ x1 := by rfl
        _ = v := hv.symm
        _ = x2 ⬝ y2 := hv'
        _ = x2 ++ y2 := by rfl
    ```

3.  **Apply Levi's lemma:**
    ```lean4
    have h_cases := (List.append_eq_append_iff).mp h_eq
    rcases h_cases with (⟨t, ht1, ht2⟩ | ⟨t, ht1, ht2⟩)
    ```
    In the first branch, `ht1 : y1 ++ t = x2` and `ht2 : x1 = t ++ y2`.
    In the second branch, `ht1 : y1 = x2 ++ t` and `ht2 : t ++ x1 = y2`.

4.  **First case (`y1 ++ t = x2` and `x1 = t ++ y2`):**
    - Provide witnesses: `X := t`, `Y := y2 ++ y1`.
    - Solve `u = X ⬝ (Y)`:
      ```lean4
      have hu_eq : u = t ++ (y2 ++ y1) := by
        calc
          u = x1 ++ y1 := hu
          _ = (t ++ y2) ++ y1 := by rw [ht2]
          _ = t ++ (y2 ++ y1) := by rw [List.append_assoc]
      ```
    - Solve `w = Y ⬝ X`:
      ```lean4
      have hw_eq : w = (y2 ++ y1) ++ t := by
        calc
          w = y2 ++ x2 := hw
          _ = y2 ++ (y1 ++ t) := by rw [ht1]
          _ = (y2 ++ y1) ++ t := by rw [← List.append_assoc]
      ```
    - Assemble the existential:
      ```lean4
      refine ⟨t, y2 ++ y1, ?_, ?_⟩
      · simpa [Word.concat] using hu_eq
      · simpa [Word.concat] using hw_eq
      ```

5.  **Second case (`y1 = x2 ++ t` and `t ++ x1 = y2`):**
    - Provide witnesses: `X := x1 ++ x2`, `Y := t`.
    - Solve `u = X ⬝ Y`:
      ```lean4
      have hu_eq : u = (x1 ++ x2) ++ t := by
        calc
          u = x1 ++ y1 := hu
          _ = x1 ++ (x2 ++ t) := by rw [ht1]
          _ = (x1 ++ x2) ++ t := by rw [← List.append_assoc]
      ```
    - Solve `w = Y ⬝ X`:
      ```lean4
      have hw_eq : w = t ++ (x1 ++ x2) := by
        calc
          w = y2 ++ x2 := hw
          _ = (t ++ x1) ++ x2 := by rw [ht2]
          _ = t ++ (x1 ++ x2) := by rw [List.append_assoc]
      ```
    - Assemble the existential:
      ```lean4
      refine ⟨x1 ++ x2, t, ?_, ?_⟩
      · simpa [Word.concat] using hu_eq
      · simpa [Word.concat] using hw_eq
      ```

6.  **Final step:** The two `refine` branches close the goal; no further tactics are needed.

[36/45]         Period |   EASY | hasPeriod_of_short

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for hasPeriod_of_short
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is to prove that any word of length ≤ 1 has period p for any positive p. The definition `HasPeriod w p` requires `0 < p` and the condition that for all i with `i + p < w.length`, the i-th and (i+p)-th letters are equal. Since `w.length ≤ 1`, the inequality `i + p < w.length` forces `i + p < 1`. With `p ≥ 1`, this is impossible, so the condition holds vacuously. The proof uses basic Nat arithmetic: `Nat.lt_one_iff` to get `i + p = 0`, then `Nat.eq_zero_of_add_eq_zero_right` to derive `p = 0`, contradicting `hp : 0 < p`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. **Begin the definition of `HasPeriod w p`.**  
   The goal is `HasPeriod w p`, which is defined as `0 < p ∧ ∀ i, i + p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`.  
   So we first split: `refine ⟨hp, ?_⟩`. Now we need to prove the `∀` statement.

2. **Introduce the universal quantifier.**  
   `intro i hi` where `hi : i + p < w.length`.

3. **Derive a contradiction from `hi` and `hw`.**  
   Since `hw : w.length ≤ 1`, we can combine: `i + p < w.length ≤ 1`, so `i + p < 1`.  
   Use `have h_lt_one : i + p < 1 := lt_of_lt_of_le hi hw`.

4. **Use `Nat.lt_one_iff` to get `i + p = 0`.**  
   The lemma `Nat.lt_one_iff` yields `i + p < 1 ↔ i + p = 0`. So  
   `have h_zero : i + p = 0 := (Nat.lt_one_iff.mp h_lt_one)`.

5. **Deduce `p = 0` from `i + p = 0`.**  
   The lemma `Nat.eq_zero_of_add_eq_zero_right` gives `p = 0`. So  
   `have hp_zero : p = 0 := Nat.eq_zero_of_add_eq_zero_right h_zero`.

6. **Contradiction with `hp : 0 < p`.**  
   `hp` is a proof that `0 < p`, which implies `p ≠ 0`. Use `hp.ne'` to get `p ≠ 0`. Then `exact (hp.ne' hp_zero).elim`.  
   Alternatively, `exfalso; exact hp.ne' hp_zero`. This closes the goal.

7. **The entire proof** (without `omega`):
   ```lean4
   refine ⟨hp, ?_⟩
   intro i hi
   have h_lt_one : i + p < 1 := lt_of_lt_of_le hi hw
   have h_zero : i + p = 0 := (Nat.lt_one_iff.mp h_lt_one)
   have hp_zero : p = 0 := Nat.eq_zero_of_add_eq_zero_right h_zero
   exfalso; exact hp.ne' hp_zero
   ```
   (You can also inline the last line with `exact (hp.ne' hp_zero).elim`.)

[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We need to prove that any word of length 1 is primitive. From the definition, `IsPrimitive w` is the conjunction: `w ≠ [] ∧ ¬ ∃ u k, k ≥ 2 ∧ w = u ^ k`. The first part follows immediately from `h : w.length = 1` using `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`. The second part is a proof by contradiction: assuming such a decomposition exists, we use `Word.length_pow` to get a length equation `1 = k * u.length`, from which `k ≥ 2` forces `u.length = 0`, implying `u = []` and thus `w = []`, contradicting `h`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. **Prove that `w ≠ []`**  
   Since `h : w.length = 1`, we have `0 < w.length`.  
   The lemma `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil` gives equivalence between `0 < List.length w` and `w ≠ []`.  
   So we can do:
   ```lean4
   have hne : w ≠ [] := by
     have hpos : 0 < w.length := by linarith [h]  -- or by omega
     simpa [Word.length] using (List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mp hpos)
   ```
   Alternatively, directly:
   ```lean4
   have hne : w ≠ [] := by
     rw [← List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil, ← h]
     exact Nat.one_pos
   ```

2. **Prove that no proper power decomposition exists**  
   We need to show `¬ ∃ u k, k ≥ 2 ∧ w = u ^ k`.  
   Proceed by contradiction:  
   ```lean4
   refine ⟨hne, ?_⟩
   rintro ⟨u, k, hk, hw_eq⟩
   ```
   Now we have `hk : k ≥ 2` and `hw_eq : w = u ^ k`.

3. **Apply the length function to the equality `hw_eq`**  
   ```lean4
   have hlen_eq := congrArg Word.length hw_eq
   ```
   Compute both sides:  
   The left-hand side is `w.length = 1` (by `h`).  
   The right-hand side by `Word.length_pow` is `(u ^ k).length = k * u.length`.  
   So we have: `1 = k * u.length`.

   To see this, use:
   ```lean4
   rw [h, Word.length_pow] at hlen_eq
   ```
   which gives `1 = k * u.length`.

4. **Derive that `u.length = 0`**  
   Since `k ≥ 2` and `u.length` is a natural number, examine possible values.  
   If `u.length ≥ 1`, then `k * u.length ≥ 2 * 1 = 2 > 1`, contradicting `hlen_eq`.  
   Therefore `u.length = 0`.  
   This can be shown by case analysis:  
   ```lean4
   have hu_len0 : u.length = 0 := by
     by_contra! hpos
     have : u.length ≥ 1 := Nat.one_le_of_lt (Nat.pos_of_ne_zero hpos)  -- if positive
     have : k * u.length ≥ 2 := by
       calc
         k * u.length ≥ 2 * u.length := Nat.mul_le_mul_right u.length hk
         _ ≥ 2 * 1 := Nat.mul_le_mul_left 2 (by omega)
         _ = 2 := by norm_num
       -- or more directly: hk : k ≥ 2, so k * u.length ≥ 2 * 1 > 1
     linarith [hlen_eq]
   ```
   Simpler: use `omega`. But with only `linarith`? We can argue: `k ≥ 2` and `u.length ≥ 1` implies `k * u.length ≥ 2 * 1 = 2 > 1`, contradiction. So `u.length = 0`.

5. **From `u.length = 0` deduce `u = []`**  
   Use `List.length_eq_zero.mp` (since `Word.length` is `List.length`):
   ```lean4
   have hu_nil : u = [] := by
     simpa [Word.length] using List.length_eq_zero.mp hu_len0
   ```

6. **Compute `u ^ k` when `u = []`**  
   The lemma `Word.one_pow` (from `Word.lean`) says `([] : Word α) ^ n = []`. So
   ```lean4
   have h_pow_nil : u ^ k = [] := by
     simp [hu_nil, Word.one_pow]
   ```
   (or `rw [hu_nil, Word.one_pow]`).

7. **Contradiction with `w.length = 1` (namely `w ≠ []`)**  
   From `hw_eq` and `h_pow_nil`, we have `w = []`. But `hne : w ≠ []`. Contradiction.
   ```lean4
   rw [h_pow_nil] at hw_eq
   exact hne hw_eq
   ```
   (alternatively, `apply hne; rw [← hw_eq, h_pow_nil]`)

8. **End** – the contradiction finishes the `¬ ∃` proof.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

     intro hnil
     rw [hnil, Word.length_empty] at h

   ```

   ```lean4

   By contradiction: assume `u.length ≠ 0`. Then `0 < u.length` by `Nat.pos_of_ne_zero`. Then `1 ≤ u.length` by `Nat.succ_le_of_lt`.
   Using `hk : 2 ≤ k` and `Nat.mul_le_mul`, we get `2 * 1 ≤ k * u.length`. Simplify `2 * 1 = 2` with `norm_num`. Hence `2 ≤ k * u.length`.
   From `hlen_eq` we have `k * u.length = 1`. Combining yields `2 ≤ 1`, which contradicts `Nat.not_succ_le_self 1`.
   ```lean4
   have hu_len0 : u.length = 0 := by
     by_contra! hpos
     have hpos' : 1 ≤ u.length :=
       Nat.succ_le_of_lt (Nat.pos_of_ne_zero hpos)
     have h_mul_ge_2 : 2 ≤ k * u.length := by
       calc
         2 = 2 * 1 := by norm_num
         _ ≤ k * u.length := Nat.mul_le_mul hk hpos'
     have : 2 ≤ 1 := by
       calc
         2 ≤ k * u.length := h_mul_ge_2
         _ = 1 := by rw [← hlen_eq]
     exact Nat.not_succ_le_self 1 this
   ```

   rw [hu_nil, Word.one_pow] at hw_eq
   ```

   `hw_eq` now says `w = []`, which contradicts `hne`.
   ```lean4
   exact hne hw_eq

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The definition `IsMinimalPeriod w p` is `HasPeriod w p ∧ ∀ q, HasPeriod w q → p ≤ q`. Thus both `hp` and `hq` assert that their respective period is minimal. From `hp` we can derive `p ≤ q` because `hq` provides evidence that `q` is a period. Symmetrically, `q ≤ p`. By `Nat.le_antisymm` we get `p = q`. No additional lemmas are required.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

   ```lean4

   ```

   ```

[39/45]         Period |   HARD | primitive_minimal_period_is_length

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for primitive_minimal_period_is_length
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem as stated is false. A primitive word can have a minimal period strictly smaller than its length. For example, `aba` (length 3) is primitive (it is not a proper power) yet has period 2, so its minimal period is 2, not 3. Therefore no proof can exist using the given hypotheses. The builder's repeated failures are consistent with this.

The correct statement involves *unbordered* words, not primitive words. A word is unbordered if it has no non‑empty border. The classical theorem is: if `w` is unbordered and `|w| ≥ 2`, then the minimal period of `w` is its length. This follows from the duality between periods and borders: if `w` has a period `q < |w|`, then the suffix of length `|w|‑q` is a border of `w`.

I will therefore provide a plan for the corrected theorem (using `IsUnbordered` instead of `IsPrimitive`). The plan uses two existing lemmas from the library:
* `hasPeriod_length` (requires only `w ≠ []`, which follows from `IsUnbordered` for length ≥ 2)
* a new (not yet in the library) lemma that from `HasPeriod w q` with `q < w.length` we can construct a border, which would contradict `IsUnbordered`. Because this lemma is missing, I will incorporate its proof idea as a sequence of steps using the definition of `IsBorder` and `HasPeriod`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
We assume the hypothesis `hborder : IsUnbordered w` (instead of `hprim`) and `hlen : w.length ≥ 2`. The goal is `IsMinimalPeriod w w.length`.

1. **Prove that `HasPeriod w w.length`**.
   Since `w.length ≥ 2`, we have `w ≠ []`. The lemma `hasPeriod_length` from `CoW.Period` gives `HasPeriod w w.length` given `w ≠ []`.
   ```lean4
   have hne : w ≠ [] := by
     intro hnil
     rw [hnil, Word.length_empty] at hlen
     linarith
   have hper : HasPeriod w w.length := hasPeriod_length hne
   ```

2. **Prove minimality: for any `q` with `HasPeriod w q`, we have `w.length ≤ q`**.
   Let `q` be arbitrary and `hq : HasPeriod w q`. We need to show `w.length ≤ q`. We argue by contradiction: assume `q < w.length`.
   From `hq` and `q < w.length`, we will construct a border of `w` of length `w.length - q`, contradicting `hborder`.
   
   - **Construct the border candidate `b`**: take `b` as the last `w.length - q` symbols of `w`. Formally, using `List.take` and `List.drop` (since `Word` is `List`). We can define `b` as `List.drop q w` (because `q + (w.length - q) = w.length`). Actually, a border is a word that is both a proper prefix and a proper suffix. The suffix of length `w.length - q` is `List.drop q w`. Its length is `w.length - q`. Since `q > 0` (from `hq.1`), this suffix is proper (not the whole word) if `q > 0`. Also we need to show that this suffix is also a prefix of `w`. That's exactly the periodicity condition: for all `i < w.length - q`, the `i`-th letter of the prefix matches the `i`-th letter of the suffix. Indeed, `w.get? i = w.get? (i + q)` by `hq.2` when `i + q < w.length`. For `i < w.length - q`, we have `i + q < w.length`. So by using `hq.2` repeatedly, we can show `List.drop q w` is a prefix of `w`. This can be proven by induction on the length. 
   
   However, a simpler route may use the classic lemma `List.append_eq_append_iff` or a known characterization of periods. Since no such lemma exists in the library, we can outline the proof:
   
   - Define `b := List.drop q w`.
   - Show that `List.length b = w.length - q`.
   - Show `b <ₚ w` (proper prefix). For that, we need `List.IsPrefix b w`. Use `List.isPrefix_iff`? The definition of `IsPrefix` in the library is `List.IsPrefix`. The condition `HasPeriod hq` ensures that the first `b.length` letters equal the last `b.length` letters. We can prove by induction on `i` that for all `i < b.length`, `(List.get? b i) = (List.get? w i)`. This implies `List.IsPrefix b w`. We can use `List.prefix_iff_take` or `List.isPrefix_iff`. The lemma `List.isPrefix_iff` states `l1 <+: l2 ↔ l1 = List.take (List.length l1) l2`. So we can prove `b = List.take (List.length b) w` by using the periodicity condition.
     * `List.length b = w.length - q`.
     * For `i < w.length - q`, `List.get? (List.take (w.length - q) w) i = List.get? w i`. And `List.get? (List.drop q w) i = List.get? w (i + q)`. By `hq.2`, if `i + q < w.length`, these are equal. Since `i < w.length - q`, we have `i + q < w.length`. Hence they match. So `List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w` as lists. So `b` is a prefix of `w`.
   - Show that `b` is also a proper suffix. By definition, `b` is the suffix starting at `q`. Since `q > 0`, it is a proper suffix (the whole word is `List.take q w ++ b`). So `b` is a proper suffix.
   - Thus `IsBorder b w`. Since `hborder` requires all borders to be empty, we get `b = []`. This forces `w.length - q = 0`, i.e. `w.length = q`, contradicting `q < w.length`.

   The proof can be laid out using `calc` and `simp` with `List` operations.

3. **From `IsUnbordered`, derive `IsMinimalPeriod`**:
   ```lean4
   refine ⟨hper, ?_⟩
   intro q hq
   by_contra! hlt   -- hlt: q < w.length
   have hborder_b : IsBorder (List.drop q w) w := ...
   have h_empty := hborder (List.drop q w) hborder_b
   have hlen_drop : (List.drop q w).length = w.length - q := List.length_drop q w
   rw [h_empty] at hlen_drop
   have : 0 = w.length - q := by simpa using hlen_drop
   omega   -- contradicts hlt
   ```

We must fill in the construction of `hborder_b`. Since this fills about half of the proof, I will describe the steps concisely.

**Constructing `IsBorder (List.drop q w) w`**:

- Let `b := List.drop q w`.
- `hb_length : b.length = w.length - q` by `List.length_drop`.
- `hq_pos : 0 < q` from `hq.1`.
- `h_prefix : b ≤ₚ w` (i.e., `List.IsPrefix b w`). To prove it:
   * Use `List.isPrefix_iff.mpr`. Need `b = List.take (List.length b) w`.
   * Since `List.length b = w.length - q`, we must show `List.drop q w = List.take (w.length - q) w`.
   * This follows by `List.drop_eq_take_of_period`? There's no such lemma. We can prove by extensionality: `List.ext` with `intro i hi`. Two cases: `i < w.length - q` or `i ≥ w.length - q`. Actually, both sides have length `w.length - q`. So we only need to check the elements for `i < w.length - q`. For such `i`, we have:
        - `List.get? (List.drop q w) i = w.get? (i+q)` by `List.get?_drop`.
        - `List.get? (List.take (w.length - q) w) i = w.get? i`.
     Now `hq.2` says for `i` with `i + q < w.length`, `w.get? i = w.get? (i+q)`. Since `i < w.length - q`, we have `i + q < w.length` (by `Nat.lt_sub_iff_add_lt` or `omega`). Therefore the two entries are equal.
   * So we get `List.drop q w = List.take (w.length - q) w`.
   * Hence `b = List.take b.length w`, giving `List.IsPrefix b w`.
- `h_suffix : b ≤ₛ w` (proper suffix): `List.drop q w` is a suffix by definition, and since `q > 0`, it is a proper suffix. Use `List.suffix_drop`? There is `List.IsSuffix_drop`. And `List.IsSuffix` instance. To show proper, need `b ≠ w`. This follows from `b.length = w.length - q < w.length` because `q>0`. So `b` is proper suffix.
- Combine to `IsBorder b w`.

Now, use `hborder` to get `b = []`. Then `w.length - q = 0`, so `w.length = q`, contradiction with `q < w.length`. Hence `w.length ≤ q`.

4. **Put everything together**:
   - The proof will require `omega` for arithmetic.
   - Some lemmas like `List.length_drop`, `List.get?_drop`, `List.get?_take`, `List.isPrefix_iff`. All from Mathlib.

Thus the full plan is:
   - Show `w ≠ []`.
   - Use `hasPeriod_length` to get `HasPeriod w w.length`.
   - For minimality:
       ```lean4
       intro q hq
       by_contra! hlt
       let b := List.drop q w
       have hlen_b : b.length = w.length - q := List.length_drop q w
       have hpre : b ≤ₚ w := by
         apply (IsPrefix.def b w).mpr
         -- need to produce some v such that w = b ++ v; but b is suffix, not prefix. Wait, `≤ₚ` is prefix: w = b ++ v. But b is a suffix, not a prefix. Actually, we claimed b is both prefix and suffix. So we need w = b ++ something? That would mean b is prefix, so we need a suffix v such that w = b ++ v. That would be wrong: b = drop q w, so w = (take q w) ++ b. So b is suffix, not prefix. I made a mistake: `IsPrefix` means `b` is a prefix of `w`. But `b` is the drop, not take. So I got it backwards. Let's re-check: In the periodic argument, if w has period q, then the prefix of length |w|-q is equal to the suffix of length |w|-q? Actually, standard: If period q, then the border (both prefix and suffix) of length |w|-q. So the border is the prefix of length |w|-q and also the suffix of length |w|-q. So we want `b` to be the prefix of length |w|-q, not the drop. The suffix of length |w|-q is equal to that prefix. So the border is the prefix of length |w|-q, which is `List.take (w.length - q) w`. This prefix is also a suffix? The periodicity ensures that this prefix appears at the end as well. So b = `List.take (w.length - q) w` is both a prefix (by definition) and a suffix (by periodicity). So we should define `b := List.take (w.length - q) w`. Then `b` is a prefix of `w` by definition. To show it's a suffix, we need to show that `w = something ++ b`. Specifically, the suffix of the same length is `List.drop q w`. The periodicity condition implies `List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w`. Thus `b` also equals `List.drop q w`, and therefore `b` is a suffix because `w = (take q w) ++ b`. So we can use `List.take` for border.

   The proper suffix condition: `b` is a suffix of `w`, and since `b.length = w.length - q < w.length` (because `q > 0`), `b ≠ w`. Hence `IsBorder b w`.

   So we need to prove `List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w`. That equality follows from the periodicity condition and can be shown using `List.ext` with `List.get?`. Then from that equality we get both the prefix and suffix properties.

Thus:

- `hperiod_eq : List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w` (call it `h_eq`).
- `h_pre : b ≤ₚ w` from `by` `apply (IsPrefix.def b w).mpr; refine ⟨List.drop q w, ?_⟩`? Wait, if `b = take ...`, then `w = b ++ (drop (w.length - q) w)`? Not needed. Simpler: `List.IsPrefix` has lemma `List.prefix_take`. There is `List.prefix_take`? Actually, `List.take_prefix`? There's `List.prefix_iff_eq_take`. But plain `List.IsPrefix` of `List.take n w` to `w` is `List.take_prefix n w`. That lemma exists: `List.take_prefix n w : List.take n w <+: w`. So we can use `List.take_prefix (w.length - q) w` to get `b ≤ₚ w`. Similarly, `List.IsSuffix (List.drop q w) w` is `List.suffix_drop q w`. But we need `b` to be a suffix. From `h_eq`, `b` equals `List.drop q w`. So `h_suffix : b ≤ₛ w` is `h_eq.symm ▸ List.suffix_drop q w`. Then `IsBorder` requires proper prefix and proper suffix. Proper prefix: `b ≠ w` because `b.length = w.length - q < w.length` (if `q>0`). Proper suffix: same.

Thus the construction is clean.

- `hq_pos : 0 < q` from `hq.1`.
- `h_lt_len : b.length < w.length` by `have hlen : b.length = w.length - q := List.length_take (w.length - q) w`? Actually, `List.length_take` gives `b.length = min (w.length - q) w.length`. Since `w.length - q ≤ w.length`, the min is `w.length - q`. So `b.length = w.length - q`. Then `h_lt_len` because `q > 0`. So `b ≠ w` by `List.length_ne_iff`? Use `List.length_lt`? There's `List.length_lt_of_ne`? Simpler: `intro heq; rw [heq] at hlen; omega`.

Now the proof steps can be outlined clearly.

```lean4
have hne : w ≠ [] := by
    intro hnil
    rw [hnil, Word.length_empty] at hlen
    omega

  have hper : HasPeriod w w.length := hasPeriod_length hne

  refine ⟨hper, ?_⟩
  intro q hq
  by_contra! hlt
  -- hlt: q < w.length
  have hqpos : 0 < q := hq.1
  set b := List.take (w.length - q) w with hb_def
  have h_len_b : b.length = w.length - q := by
    dsimp [b]
    rw [List.length_take]
    exact min_eq_left (by omega)
  have h_prefix : b ≤ₚ w := by
    rw [hb_def]
    exact (IsPrefix.def _ _).mpr ⟨List.drop (w.length - q) w, by simp [List.take_append_drop]⟩
  have h_eq : List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w := by
    apply List.ext
    intro i
    by_cases hi : i < w.length - q
    · have hi_add : i + q < w.length := by omega
      have htake : (List.take (w.length - q) w).get? i = w.get? i := by
        rw [List.get?_take]
        exact if_pos hi
      have hdrop : (List.drop q w).get? i = w.get? (q + i) := by
        rw [List.get?_drop]
      have hper := hq.2 i hi_add
      -- hper: w.get? i = w.get? (i + q)
      rw [htake, hdrop, hper, add_comm q i]
    · have htake : (List.take (w.length - q) w).get? i = none := by
        apply List.get?_eq_none.mpr
        rw [List.length_take]
        have hsub : w.length - q ≤ w.length := by omega
        rw [min_eq_left hsub]
        omega
      have hdrop : (List.drop q w).get? i = none := by
        apply List.get?_eq_none.mpr
        rw [List.length_drop]
        omega
      rw [htake, hdrop]
  have h_suffix : b ≤ₛ w := by
    rw [hb_def, h_eq]
    exact (IsSuffix.def _ _).mpr ⟨List.take q w, by simp [List.take_append_drop]⟩
  have h_proper_prefix : b <ₚ w := by
    refine ⟨h_prefix, ?_⟩
    intro heq
    have h_len_eq : b.length = w.length := by simpa [heq]
    rw [h_len_b] at h_len_eq
    omega
  have h_proper_suffix : b <ₛ w := by
    refine ⟨h_suffix, ?_⟩
    intro heq
    have h_len_eq : b.length = w.length := by simpa [heq]
    rw [h_len_b] at h_len_eq
    omega
  have hborder_b : IsBorder b w := ⟨h_proper_prefix, h_proper_suffix⟩
  have h_empty := hborder b hborder_b
  rw [hb_def] at h_empty
  have h_len_take : (List.take (w.length - q) w).length = w.length - q := by
    rw [List.length_take]
    exact min_eq_left (by omega)
  rw [h_empty] at h_len_take
  simp at h_len_take
  omega
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The duality between periods and borders tells us that if a word has a period `q < |w|`, then the prefix of length `|w| - q` is a non‑empty border. Since `w` is unbordered, no such border exists; hence the minimal period is `|w|`.

The proof will:
1. Show `HasPeriod w w.length` using `hasPeriod_length` (needs `w ≠ []`, which follows from `2 ≤ w.length`).
2. For minimality, assume a period `q` with `q < w.length`, construct a non‑empty border using `List.take (w.length - q) w`, and derive a contradiction.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. **Non‑emptiness**: from `hlen : 2 ≤ w.length` we obtain `hne : w ≠ []`.
   ```lean4
   have hne : w ≠ [] := by
     intro he; rw [he, Word.length_empty] at hlen; omega
   ```

2. **Base period**: `hasPeriod_length hne` gives `HasPeriod w w.length`.
   ```lean4
   have hper : HasPeriod w w.length := hasPeriod_length hne
   ```

3. **Minimality**: we need `∀ q, HasPeriod w q → w.length ≤ q`. Introduce `q` and `hq : HasPeriod w q`. Prove `w.length ≤ q` by contradiction.
   ```lean4
   refine ⟨hper, ?_⟩
   intro q hq
   by_contra! hlt      -- hlt : q < w.length
   have hq_pos : 0 < q := hq.1
   ```

4. **Construct the candidate border**: let `b := List.take (w.length - q) w`.
   - Its length is `w.length - q`.
   - Because `q > 0`, we have `b.length < w.length`, so `b ≠ w`.
   - By definition, `b` is a prefix of `w` (lemma `List.take_prefix` gives `List.IsPrefix b w`).

5. **Prove that `b` is also a suffix**: we need `b ≤ₛ w`. The periodicity condition `hq` implies that the prefix of length `w.length - q` equals the suffix of the same length, i.e. `List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w`. We prove this equality using `List.ext` with `List.get?` and the hypothesis `hq.2`. 

   *Lemma*: `List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w`.
   - For each `i`, compare `List.get?` of both sides.
   - If `i < w.length - q`, then `i + q < w.length`. By `hq.2`, `w.get? i = w.get? (i + q)`. Also `List.get?_take` gives `(take ... w).get? i = w.get? i` and `List.get?_drop` gives `(drop q w).get? i = w.get? (i + q)`. Thus equal.
   - If `i ≥ w.length - q`, then both sides return `none` (since their lengths are `w.length - q`).
   So we have equality.

   Call this equality `h_eq : List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w`.

6. **Suffix property**: using `h_eq`, we rewrite `b` to `List.drop q w`. The lemma `List.suffix_drop q w` gives `List.IsSuffix (List.drop q w) w`. Hence `b ≤ₛ w`. Use `(IsSuffix.def _ _).mpr` with witness `List.take q w` (since `w = (take q w) ++ (drop q w)` by `List.take_append_drop`).

7. **Proper prefix/suffix**: 
   - `h_prefix : b ≤ₚ w` from `List.take_prefix`.
   - `h_suffix : b ≤ₛ w` from step 6.
   - Since `b.length = w.length - q` (by `List.length_take` and the inequality), and `q > 0`, we have `b.length < w.length`. Hence `b ≠ w`. This gives properness:
     ```lean4
     have h_ne : b ≠ w := by
       intro he; have := congrArg List.length he; rw [h_len_b] at this; omega
     ```
   - So `h_proper_prefix : b <ₚ w := ⟨h_prefix, h_ne⟩` and `h_proper_suffix : b <ₛ w := ⟨h_suffix, h_ne⟩`.

8. **Border**: `IsBorder b w := ⟨h_proper_prefix, h_proper_suffix⟩`.
   Apply `hunb` to this border: `hunb b this` gives `b = []`.

9. **Contradiction**: from `b = []` and `b.length = w.length - q`, we deduce `w.length - q = 0`, i.e. `w.length = q`, which contradicts `q < w.length`.
   ```lean4
   have h_len_b : b.length = w.length - q := by
     dsimp [b]; rw [List.length_take, min_eq_left (by omega : w.length - q ≤ w.length)]
   rw [hb_empty, List.length_nil] at h_len_b
   omega
   ```
   This contradiction closes the inner `by_contra!`, establishing `w.length ≤ q`.

10. **Conclusion**: `IsMinimalPeriod w w.length` is proved.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 3/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The statement “A primitive word's minimal period equals its length” is **false**. A counterexample: the word `aba` (length 3) is primitive (it is not a proper power) but has period 2, so its minimal period is 2, not 3. Therefore no proof can exist for the given hypotheses `IsPrimitive w` and `w.length ≥ 2`. The builder correctly identified this.

To obtain a valid theorem, one must replace `IsPrimitive` with `IsUnbordered`. The corrected statement is:

```lean4
theorem unbordered_minimal_period_is_length {w : Word α}
    (hunb : IsUnbordered w) (hlen : 2 ≤ w.length) : IsMinimalPeriod w w.length :=
```

The proof of the corrected statement uses the classical period‑border duality: if `q` is a period with `q < |w|`, then the prefix of length `|w|‑q` is a non‑empty border, contradicting `IsUnbordered`. All necessary lemmas (`hasPeriod_length`, `List.take_prefix`, `List.suffix_drop`, `List.length_take`, `List.length_drop`, `List.get?_take`, `List.get?_drop`, `List.ext`, `omega`) are already in the library.

Since the original statement is false, I cannot provide a valid plan for it. The only honest plan is to change the hypothesis to `IsUnbordered`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
The original theorem is unprovable because it is false. The correct formulation uses `IsUnbordered`. Therefore the plan must first **replace** the statement with the corrected one. The steps for the corrected proof are:

1. **Non‑emptiness**: From `hlen : 2 ≤ w.length`, deduce `w ≠ []` (by `omega` using `Word.length_empty`).
2. **Base period**: Apply `hasPeriod_length` (from `CoW.Period`) to get `HasPeriod w w.length`.
3. **Minimality**: For any `q` with `HasPeriod w q`, assume `q < w.length` and derive a contradiction by constructing a non‑empty border.
   - `hq.1` gives `0 < q`.
   - Define `b := List.take (w.length - q) w`.
   - `b` is a prefix by `List.take_prefix`.
   - Show `List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w` using `List.ext` and `hq.2` (periodicity condition). This equality is the key step; it uses `List.get?_take`, `List.get?_drop`, and `hq.2` to equate elementwise, handling index bounds with `omega`.
   - From the equality, `b` also equals a suffix, so `b ≤ₛ w` via `List.suffix_drop` (or `(IsSuffix.def _ _).mpr` with witness `List.take q w`).
   - Compute `b.length = w.length - q` (by `List.length_take` and `min_eq_left` because `w.length - q ≤ w.length`). Because `q > 0`, we have `b.length < w.length`, so `b ≠ w`. This yields `b <ₚ w` and `b <ₛ w`.
   - Hence `IsBorder b w`. Apply `hunb b` to this fact to obtain `b = []`.
   - Then `(w.length - q) = 0`, so `w.length = q`, contradicting `q < w.length`.
4. **Conclusion**: `w.length ≤ q` holds for all periods `q`, so `IsMinimalPeriod w w.length`.

The needed lemmas are all present in the provided context; no new imports or axioms are required. The original false statement cannot be proved; the correction is mandatory.

```lean4
have hne : w ≠ [] := by
    intro hnil
    rw [hnil, Word.length_empty] at hlen
    omega
  have hper : HasPeriod w w.length := hasPeriod_length hne
  refine ⟨hper, ?_⟩
  intro q hq
  by_contra! hlt
  -- hlt: q < w.length
  have hqpos : 0 < q := hq.1
  set b := List.take (w.length - q) w with hb_def
  have h_len_b : b.length = w.length - q := by
    dsimp [b]
    rw [List.length_take]
    exact min_eq_left (by omega)
  have h_prefix : b ≤ₚ w := by
    rw [hb_def]
    exact (IsPrefix.def _ _).mpr ⟨List.drop (w.length - q) w, by simp [List.take_append_drop]⟩
  have h_eq : List.take (w.length - q) w = List.drop q w := by
    apply List.ext
    intro i
    simp only [List.getElem?_take, List.getElem?_drop]
    by_cases hi : i < w.length - q
    · have hi_add : i + q < w.length := by omega
      have hper_i := hq.2 i hi_add
      simp [hi, hper_i, add_comm q i]
    · have h_none : w.get? (q + i) = none :=
        List.getElem?_eq_none_iff.mpr (by omega)
      simp [hi, h_none]
  have h_suffix : b ≤ₛ w := by
    rw [hb_def, h_eq]
    exact (IsSuffix.def _ _).mpr ⟨List.take q w, by simp [List.take_append_drop]⟩
  have h_proper_prefix : b <ₚ w := by
    refine ⟨h_prefix, ?_⟩
    intro heq
    have h_len_eq : b.length = w.length := by simpa [heq]
    rw [h_len_b] at h_len_eq
    omega
  have h_proper_suffix : b <ₛ w := by
    refine ⟨h_suffix, ?_⟩
    intro heq
    have h_len_eq : b.length = w.length := by simpa [heq]
    rw [h_len_b] at h_len_eq
    omega
  have hborder_b : IsBorder b w := ⟨h_proper_prefix, h_proper_suffix⟩
  have h_empty := hborder b hborder_b
  rw [hb_def] at h_empty
  have h_len_take : (List.take (w.length - q) w).length = w.length - q := by
    rw [List.length_take]
    exact min_eq_left (by omega)
  rw [h_empty] at h_len_take
  simp at h_len_take
  omega
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The morphism `(fun a => Word.letter a)` maps each letter `a` to `[a]`. Applying it to a word `w` via `applyMorphism` (i.e., `flatMap`) yields `w` itself. The lemma `List.bind_singleton` from Mathlib proves exactly `l.bind (fun x => [x]) = l`. Since `applyMorphism` is `flatMap`, which is the same as `bind`, the proof is immediate.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. **Unfold the notations**: `applyMorphism` is defined as `w.flatMap f`. So the goal `(fun a => Word.letter a) •w w = w` becomes `w.flatMap (fun a => Word.letter a) = w`. Since `Word.letter a` is `[a]`, the left-hand side is `w.flatMap (fun a => [a])`.

2. **Use the list identity**: `List.flatMap (fun a => [a]) w = w`. In Mathlib, `List.flatMap` is `List.bind`, and the lemma `List.bind_singleton` states `l.bind (fun a => [a]) = l`. So we can apply it.

3. **Provide the proof**:
   ```lean4
   simpa [applyMorphism, Word.letter] using List.bind_singleton w
   ```
   This correctly unfolds the definitions and applies the lemma.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The proof is a direct composition of three existing lemmas: `applyMorphism_pow` for commuting the morphism with powers, `Word.length_pow` for the length of a power, and `IsUniform.length_image` for the length of the image of a uniform morphism. Simple arithmetic associativity (`mul_assoc`) finishes the calculation.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. **Rewrite the morphism of a power** using `applyMorphism_pow f w n`:
   ```lean4
   rw [applyMorphism_pow f w n]
   ```
   The goal becomes `((f •w w) ^ n).length = n * w.length * k`.

2. **Rewrite the length of a power** using `Word.length_pow (f •w w) n`:
   ```lean4
   rw [Word.length_pow (f •w w) n]
   ```
   The goal becomes `n * (f •w w).length = n * w.length * k`.

3. **Apply the uniform morphism length lemma** `IsUniform.length_image hf w` to replace `(f •w w).length`:
   ```lean4
   rw [IsUniform.length_image hf w]
   ```
   The goal is now `n * (w.length * k) = n * w.length * k`.

4. **Use associativity of multiplication** to align the right‑hand side:
   ```lean4
   rw [mul_assoc]
   ```
   This rewrites `n * (w.length * k)` to `(n * w.length) * k`, which matches `n * w.length * k` by left‑associativity of `*`. The goal becomes `(n * w.length) * k = (n * w.length) * k`, which is true by `rfl`. Alternatively, `simp [mul_assoc]` or `ring` would also work.

5. **No further steps**; the chain of rewrites concludes the proof.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We can obtain the equality by combining three lemmas:
- `applyMorphism_pow` to distribute the morphism across the power,
- `Word.length_pow` to expand the length of a power,
- `IsUniform.length_image` to compute the length of the image of a uniform morphism.
The resulting expression `n * (w.length * k)` is then associatively equal to the goal’s right‑hand side `n * w.length * k`. Using a `calc` block makes each step explicit and avoids potential `rw` under a binder or ambiguous notation issues.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

   ```lean4

     (f •w (w ^ n)).length = ((f •w w) ^ n).length := by rw [applyMorphism_pow f w n]
     _ = n * (f •w w).length := by rw [Word.length_pow]
     _ = n * (w.length * k) := by rw [IsUniform.length_image hf w]
     _ = n * w.length * k := by rw [mul_assoc]
   ```
   - The first step uses `applyMorphism_pow` to push the morphism inside the power.
   - The second step uses `Word.length_pow` to replace the length of a power.
   - The third step uses `IsUniform.length_image` to compute the image length.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We need to prove that the composition of two non‑erasing morphisms is non‑erasing. By definition, `IsNonErasing (compMorphism g f)` means `∀ a, (compMorphism g f) a ≠ []`. Since `(compMorphism g f) a = g •w (f a)`, the goal reduces to `g •w (f a) ≠ []`. This follows directly from the previously proven lemma `nonErasing_preserves_ne_empty`, using `hf a : f a ≠ []` and the hypothesis `hg : IsNonErasing g`.

   `IsNonErasing (compMorphism g f)` expands to `∀ a, (compMorphism g f) a ≠ []`.
   `compMorphism g f a` expands to `g •w (f a)`.

The composition of two non‑erasing morphisms is non‑erasing because applying a non‑erasing morphism to any non‑empty word yields a non‑empty word. This is exactly the content of the already‑proven lemma `nonErasing_preserves_ne_empty`. We can thereby avoid any induction over the internal structure of `f a`.

1. **Introduce the argument `a`** (the goal is `∀ a, ...`):
   ```lean4
   intro a
   ```

   ```lean4

   ```
   The goal becomes `g •w (f a) ≠ []`.

3. **Apply the lemma `nonErasing_preserves_ne_empty`**:
   This lemma has the signature `(hg : IsNonErasing g) → (hw : w ≠ []) → g •w w ≠ []`.

   exact nonErasing_preserves_ne_empty hg (hf a)
   ```
   Alternatively, combine everything:
   ```lean4

The goal `IsNonErasing (compMorphism g f)` is equivalent to:
`∀ a, g •w (f a) ≠ []`.
The lemma `nonErasing_preserves_ne_empty` (already present in the library) states exactly that if `h : IsNonErasing g` and `w ≠ []` then `g •w w ≠ []`. Thus for each `a`, we can apply this lemma with `w := f a` (which is non‑empty because `hf a`). No induction on `f a` is necessary, which avoids the previous syntactic pitfalls.
